of the world should be worried. They are on notice that Sally is back, the old Sally Pearson is back again, Australia's head coach Craig Hilliard has warned.\n\nAustralians are often given to hubris about their sportspeople, but in this case Hilliard sounds measured and almost understated.\n\nAfter about two years lost to injury Sally Pearson has defied her own expectations and found her way back among the world's best.\n\nWhile she has been gone people have run faster yet won nothing, another has won everything but lost even more through a drug ban, a long-time rival has lingered on but served a drug ban in between times.\n\nThey have all done things, remarkable and unremarkable, virtuous and without virtue or class. They have, in the case of Kendra Harrison, broken the world record but never won anything when something important was on the line. An athlete who can run to break records but not win races is not a runner not a racer.\n\nSally was, and is, both. When she raced in 2011, 2012 and 2013 she beat the clock and the field. She ran fast, but first and foremost she ran to win.\n\nAdvertisement\n\nThat is the characteristic that Hilliard was speaking to when he offered the hyperbolic warning that Australia's best athlete should be feared.\n\nIn part it is coach rhetoric to talk like a wild-haired boxing promoter at a weigh-in but Hilliard was speaking with balance about Pearson. Quite reasonably, it might be said, she is capable of anything from here.\n\nYou will now receive updates from Sport Newsletter Sport Newsletter\n\nGet the latest news and updates emailed straight to your inbox.\n\nBy submitting your email you are agreeing to Fairfax Media's terms and conditions and privacy policy .\n\n\"Sally did her last session yesterday and luckily we got some good weather and it was great, she is ready to go,\" Hilliard said.\n\n\"Since the Diamond League (she ran 12.48 seconds in London) she had two more races after that which weren't exactly around what she wanted but since then some of her training she has got through has been scintillating.\"\n\nSo in that sort of form, what do you think Craig? Should they be worried?\n\n\"Absolutely. She's an Olympic gold medallist, a world championship gold medallist, nearly broke the world record in Daegu, so that's Sally. She is confident in her ability at the moment, she is in a really good space and her warm-up yesterday was fantastic so she's ready to go.\n\n\"Go back and watch any of her runs, the London Diamond League and any of her previous major championship performances, Sally is a major championships performer, that is what she has got going for her, so they should fear Sally\n\n\"I think she can (get amongst them), absolutely and more importantly Sally believes she can.\"\n\nThe last comment is the most poignant, for self-belief is critical even in an athlete such as Sally.\n\nHer turning point on this road back from injury most fundamentally came when she ran well in London and realised she was not kidding herself - she was quick again.\n\nThe first key moment came when she parted with her previous coach. When as a coach you inherit an athlete such as Sally the temptation is to prove your value by making changes, but Sally was understood to feel she was making changes for changes' sake.\n\nSo she sacked the coach and did her own thing. She realised that after more than a decade in the sport she did not need someone else to help her get fit, she could do that on her own.\n\nThe gulf between how Sally trains and how other Aussie athletes - or athletes from anywhere really - train is clear when you watch Sally out on the track. She works incredibly hard.\n\nShe just needed someone else at certain moments to cast a critical eye over her technique in getting over the hurdles.\n\nSo she worked with Hilliard on getting the right people around her as a sounding board when it came to the technical part of her racing.\n\nShe liked the arrangement, she was a mature woman taking charge. She trusted those advising on her technical run and she trusted herself to be fit. And she is fit.\n\nIs she fit enough or fast enough? That will be tested on Friday, but the evidence suggests she is back where she was. Will that be fast enough against the world's best? Sally is not sure either, but she is more confident now than any time over the past three years.\n\n\"I'm here and I'm healthy, I'm fast, I'm fit and I'm strong ... probably just as strong as I have been when I've been at my best,\" Pearson said.", "timeCrawl": "01:36:00", "sim": 0.3725490272045135, "extractedDates": null, "location": null, "originalArticle": null, "date": "2017-08-10", "id": "8302371", "categories": [{"uri": "dmoz/Sports/Running", "label": "dmoz/Sports/Running", "id": 385, "wgt": 100}, {"uri": "dmoz/Sports/College_and_University", "label": "dmoz/Sports/College and University", "id": 562, "wgt": 100}, {"uri": "dmoz/Sports/Cycling/Racing", "label": "dmoz/Sports/Cycling/Racing", "id": 824, "wgt": 100}, {"uri": "dmoz/Health/Fitness", "label": "dmoz/Health/Fitness", "id": 1028, "wgt": 100}], "details": {}}
